<Author>Kovanen
<Content>Beware Lagoon View Rooms... Noise plus minimal view make these rooms ones to avoid.The Lagoon View rooms are an upgrade option. For that upgrade you get a slight view of the Hilton Hawaiian Village Lagoon, but only if you stand out on your balcony. Otherwise, you will be staring directly across at the tower from the Hilton Hawaiian.But the bigger problem is the noise. The Tapa Room bar at the Hilton Hawaiian plays music so loudly that you can not avoid it...close your windows and drapes and it still is louder than the TV. There is no possibility of a nice evening on the lanai.The Tapa Room thankfully winds down at about 11pm or so. But until then there will be no sleep at the Illikai from the Lagoon View rooms.-----The Ilikai gives every impression of suffering from budget issues. A minimal staff tries their best to cope, even with the hotel at only 70% occupancy this Christmas holiday. They mean well, but it is a strain.-----The hotel was clean and fresh and otherwise was a good value. It has been recently remodeled so that it shows few signs of being over 40 years old.  
<Date>Dec 29, 2008

<Author>marenostrum
<Content>Renter BEWARE Ilikai Condos Unit 684 Background- My wife and I wanted something with relative proximity to Waikiki Beach and at a reasonable price given what Honolulu can offer. Also, we love to walk and did not necessarily need to be beach front.Location- We rented a condo on the 6th floor (unit 684). The location of the condo section of the Ilikai is on the west side of Waikiki beach past the Hitlon Hawaiian village. It is in front of a marina; but given the large amount of construction the area is not very appealing. But once you are away from it, you have access to all that is available at Waikiki.Advantages- good location even if at the extreme end of Waikiki. The Hilton Hotel with the lagoon is less than 1/2 mile and a great walk is all the way to Kapiolani Park next to Diamond Head (about 2-3 miles). And walking distance to several good restaurants. Great views of the marina and harbor.Disadvantages- the condo was tired and old. Stained rugs, old appliances and flooring that needs replacing. It is above the Chart House restaurant and the street noise is easily heard, includng the music.Suggestions- when renting a condo ask for photos of the interior of the unit, last rennovation etc. We would select a higher floor above 12+ (up to 16) in much better shap. Do not rent this one # 684

<Author>monkey24
<Content>Great stay! Would come back again After a horrific one night stay at the Waikiki Gateway Hotel (which I do not recommend to anyone!) we decided to stay the remainder of our trip at the Iikai. The rooms were large with a nice comfy bed! We had a great view of the beach. Although there was construction going on behind the hotel we could not hear it. There was a fridge, ironing board, great little sitting area and lots of closet space. I would recommend that if you have a car to park it across the street as the parking at the hotel is expensive. Although it may be a bit farther from the main shopping and beach area that for the price it is well worth it. This is my third time in Oahu and I must advise if you do not like dirty old hotels then yes you will have to spend a little more as most of the hotels in Oahu have not been renovated. Our friends stayed at the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani and I must say that our room at the Iikia was much nicer, larger and a lot cheaper. I would definitely return.

<Content>Great place! Loved it! Just returned from a trip to Hawaii and we stayed four nights at the Ilikai. Two nights at beginning of trip, two nights at end of trip. <Author>candigroovez
<Content>Honeymoon from Hell First off, I was surprised to see that this hotel had reviews that were way different than mine. This hotel was horrible.I recently came back from my honeymoon which we stayed for 7nights @ The Ilikai. We were expecting a 4star hotel where we could relax and have a good time in Waikiki. BIG MISTAKE1. The first two days we stayed at the hotel, we were rudely awakened at 830am by an emergency alarm system that went off for over 10 minutes. When we called the front desk, the worker said, Yeah, we know. We're working on it. No apology for the inconvenience or explanation as to what was going on.2. Upon looking over the TV guide, we noticed there were movies out that could be purchased. (typical at a hotel). But to our dismay, no movies could be ordered at that time due to some maintenance they were doing to their system.3. They had a tiny pool with no jacuzzi. What's a honeymoon without some leisure time in the spa??4. The hotel desk said they made a manager's decision to eliminate room service at the hotel. So the only options were to go to their overpriced restaurant that did not offer delivery.5. Housekeeping failed to clean our room 3 out of 7 days we stayed there. We had to call the front desk to send someone to our room so it could be clean.6. At checkout time when we got our bill, there was an outrageous $400 phone charge for calls that were never made from our room. I admitted to the concierge that on a few occasions, I tried to reach my husband on his cellphone, only to reach an error message and a dial tone. The manager agreed to look into it. She then called me back to tell me she could not take off the charges, but she would cut it in half. When I told her that it was crazy for her to charge me for calls I didnt make, she said I'm sorry, but we have top-of-the-line phone system and you must have made the calls. So not only did they charge me, she accused me of making 30-something long-distance calls!!I would NEVER recommend using this hotel when staying in Waikiki. There were several other hotels on Ala Moana that we could have stayed at, at a much better price and with more accommodations. Our honeymoon was ruined and our wallets were badly hurt by THE HORRIBLE ILIKAI HOTEL!!

<Author>4Gs
<Content>Great Value Stayed in a Ocean Lagoon Kitchen room for $150 a night. When we arrived they tried to get me to upgrade to a newly remodeled room. This room was nice and clean. Kitchen was good other than it was missing dish soap and the pan was not non-stick. Great location though. It overlooks the marina and is close to the beach. Pool is decent. Definitely recommend this for this rate. Would have likely be willing to pay $200. We ate a Roy's. It was expensive but well worth it. We were able to walk to Roy's and pretty much everything else so a car is not necessary. Cab was $40 from the airport so would recommend shuttles for $9 a person. We did the Hawaiian Fire surf lesson-highly recommended. The will pick you up. I also strongly recommend a trip to Honolulu Hanauma Bay Nature Preserve. I would recommend this for novice snokelers as it is the best I have done from the beach. I saw a lot of fish and follow turtles near the right side of the beach for abput 45 minutes. Take a lunch because they don't have food at the bottom.

<Author>kkwj
<Content>Great for our family My husband and 2 college age children stayed in an Ocean View Kitchen unit and had a wonderful experience. What I want in a hotel is a clean room, comfortable bed, lots of space to move around, a space to grab a meal on the go (like breakfast when the shower is up for grabs!), and a convenient location. We were not looking to hang out at the pool/bar, or room service, so the fact that these facilities were not yet upgraded or even absent did not affect our stay at all. The Hilton was next door, and some of the amenities we lacked, they offered from the beach side. The concierge was extremely helpful any time I needed her. The valets were very fast retrieving our car. The location was wonderful, and only a short and enjoyable walk to the heart of Waikiki. If construction in the area and lack of amenities puts you off, then this is not for you. But if you are looking for a clean, convenient and spacious room to home base in, this is a great choice for the money.

I paid the room in full including the valet parking on the fourth day of my trip. On 7/9/08, the day before I was to leave, I called my credit card account to check to see if the $500 hold had been released and I was informed that the $500 hold and a new $400 hold was on my credit card accont. I was in shock. I went done to the desk and they acted as if they didn't know how it happened. I made them call my bank at home. Unfortunately I am from the East Coast and my bank was closing in 10 minutes so all they could do was have the hotel fax a letter to release all $900 in holds from my account. I was in tears and all the front desk and manager would say as I'm sorry. I would never stay at this hotel again. I would never recommend this hotel to anyone either. There are a lot of other hotels in the area for the same price or a little more. The Hilton is just down the street from the Ilikai and it is beautiful!!

<Author>TomVD
<Content>Well worth the money My wife and I stayed at the Ilikai from the fifth of June through the twelfth. We were both impressed by the courteous staff, the overall appearance of the hotel, and the on-site Expedia desk, which we used to plan our daily adventures. Our room was very comfortable and rather roomy for Wakiki standards. The walk to the lagoon and farther on to the beach was pleasant and never a burden. The overall location of the hotel was fabulous. We both enjoy walking so we were right at home. Ala Moana shopping center was about ten minutes away as was the International Marketplace and its surrounding shops and other venues. There are also many restaurants less than five minutes' walk (The Charthouse, Outback, Red Lobster etc...) so don't be scared off by the location at all.As has been noted here, the hotel is undergoing renovations, which really makes me want to return upon their completion. The elevators are very slow, which can be annoying and inconvenient, but allow enough time and expect the delays. The few times you won't have to wait will be pleasant surprises! Other peeves we had included the $35 per day maid service tacked on if you actually want new linens or the floors vacumed or swept, and the inner courtyard was cordened off for almost the entire week we stayed at the Ilikai.One note of caution: if you use the Expedia desk, don't fall for the no pressure and respectful time share pitch to save $100 off of your excursions' bill. The so-called real estate agents are pushy, somewhat abrasive, and definitely don't take no for an answer. Basically, they expect you to make a $40,000 decision on the spot after a two-hour presentation.Overall, we very much enjoyed our stay at the Ilikai. We Priceline(d) it ( for approximately half of the listed price on the Internet) and saved a lot of money without sacrificing anything.

<Author>Love2travelAustralia
<Content>loved this hotel We have just spent 8 days at this hotel, and couldn't have been happier. We asked for an Oceanview room with kitchen, above the 12th floor, and that is what we got. We were on the 22nd floor, and looked sideways off our balcony to the lagoon from the hotel next to us, and the Ocean. The day we arrived, we couldn't find my credit card to put the total cost on, so the receptionist offered to put the first two days onto another card we had on us. I knew I had my card, but it was in my luggage. The check in time is 3pm, but we arrived at 10.30am, and we went straight up to our room. Heaven!!! The shuttle bus we had booked online - Holoholo - was a little slow arriving at the airport, but we contacted them, and they said they were on their way. The driver couldn't have been nicer. He was very knowledgeable about Australia, which was a surprise to us, and when we asked if we would be receiving our leis, as stated on the website, and confirmed when they rang us, (only if the supply was available though), were told that, no he didn't have any. What he did do though, was drive around to a lei stall, and buy us two leis out of his own money. Now to us, this was just a wonderful gesture from this driver. They were absolutely beautiful, and the smell from them was divine. He gave us some paper towels to mop up the water on them, so we didn't get wet from them. I'm sorry that we didn't get the drivers name to give to you, but it was only my husband and I and another lady that he picked up. Not a bus that had about 20 passengers, all needing to be dropped off before you got to your hotel.There is construction going on, another highrise, next to the Hotel, but it never woke us up in the morning, and we were gone most of each day anyway. It was actually interesting seeing how they build something this size. If we had been on a much lower floor, it wouldn't have been quite so nice.We had a huge room, with a kingsize bed, big bathroom, kitchen, with a stove, microwave and full sized fridge. There was also a two seater lounge, a desk, another little coffee table, and another single seater lounge with a footstool. Our towels were changed every day, and if we had to rush out in the morning and hadn't washed our breakfast dishes, they were done when we got back to our room. We did ask for a new doona/duvet, one day, and they rang through to housekeeping while we were walking away from the front desk. There was a fresh one on the bed when we returned that day.Being at the Marina end of Waikiki was great. We were within walking distance to the Ala Moana Shopping Centre, and we actually did walk all the way to Waikiki beach and back. I would like to thank the person who advised about parking for free at the marina as well. We had read your review before we left Australia, and found out what we needed to know, so thank you. We parked the car later in the day, and were gone by the next morning, so we were never there for 24 hours, which is the restriction.There were two gift shops in the foyer, but one of them was closing down. It didn't worry us at all. Actually my husband bought a beautiful shirt, and so did I, at the one which is still open. Yes, maybe it is sad if you knew what the hotel looked like years ago, but there are hundreds of souvenir shops everywhere you look, so not having them there for you, just meant a little walk to find that perfect gift. We bought our groceries on our first day at the ABC store which is to the left as you come out the entrance of the hotel. Everything we wanted for snacks, drinks, breakfast, and tea/coffee etc. There is another ABC store to the right of the entrance of the hotel, but this one is a bit smaller. It still stocked the necessities though. This one you didn't need to cross the main road for, so it was a little easier, and quicker to get to.During my research, we discovered a Foodland store in Ala Moana Shopping Centre. We bought our meat there, and whatever else we couldn't buy at ABC. We also bought a kettle, as the coffee maker in the room didn't heat the water very well. It wasn't a problem though. We could have used the microwave if we wanted to, to heat the water. The kettle was only $8 though, so it wasn't a problem.We read some reviews about the lifts being slow. Well, yes, sometimes they were, but other times they arrived straight away. Unless there was a fire, I couldn't see a problem with having to wait anyway. We actually got into some conversations with other guests while waiting, so we passed the time. There is a bathers elevator if you just couldn't stand and wait. Sometimes they came quickly, other times, not.There was also a washing machine on our floor, along with a dryer, and ice machine, and drink machine all in the same room. The cost was $1.75 to wash, and $1.75 for the dryer. The soap dispensing machine wasn't working, but I had bought a bottle of detergent anyway, so it didn't worry me.The Gym was a 24 hour access one. It had three treadmills, two bikes, and a cross trainer, (like skiing), as well as other torture machines. There was a big container with cold water, and also towels that you could use. What a way to exercise, looking out at the Ocean. There was also a shower and toilet as well. The Pool was lovely too. You had to give them your room number before you pulled up a deckchair, which was good, as you don't want anyone walking in to use the pool. The first 15 minutes of every hour is for the Adults which I thought was a good idea, too.The walkway to the beach was very handy as well. It took you right round the Lagoon, and then you just kept going for the beach.

<Author>jstanek051
<Content>My first stay at the Ilikai - it was great. Ilikai HotelMy wife and I stayed at the Ilikai for a week in mid February. We have no complaints. We had requested a room with two double beds, but that was not possible until our third night, so the hotel put us on the fourth floor with a partial ocean view. There was construction next door when we arrived, but the workers went home at 5:00 and it was quiet. They did not return to work until Tuesday. The room had a king and a sleeper sofa, both very comfortable. The room was large, and they cleaned the room, including dirty dishes, as soon as we left. Birds on the balcony left reminders that they were there, the room cleaner even cleaned thatOn the third day we were moved to the 21st floor with a city view. Although this was noisier, if you close the door you cannot hear the traffic. The views at night were beautiful of the city skyline, and you could check the morning traffic situation before leaving. When we had the ocean view, it was great during the day (when we were not in the room) but at night, the ocean was dark, so who cares if you have an ocean view? You can see it anyway.Now the elevators. We seldom had to wait any extraordinary time for an elevator. I have stayed in hotels and worked in tall buildings, and the wait was ormal? Yes, during the morning ush?hour when everybody is trying to leave, it stopped at a lot of floors, but at almost every floor someone had pushed the button. During midday or evening they moved at a nice pace.The hotel is clean and simple and well cared for. The help in the lobby and on the phone was responsive and friendly. The fact that the only operating restaurant was on the top floor did not bother us. Hawaii is a vacation destination. If you eat at hotel restaurants, you need to get a life. Get out and check the cuisine of the Island. There is a Pub around the corner with happy hour, fast food, small mom and pop restaurants and chains within walking distance and free transport to take you to any food you want.We went across the street to the ABC convenience store and bought some snacks and ice cream and kept them in the room refrigerator and freezer. We usually arrived back in our room after dinner, and if we wanted something, it was what we had purchased ourselves, and not had to pay the overpriced changes for a tocked?mini refrigerator. You know, the $2 candy bar and $4 bottles of water.We never went to the hotel pool. We were in Hawaii, surrounded by water. Unlimited beaches, lagoons, water parks. We had a great time finding little beaches. Besides Waikiki beach, we went to Lanikai Beach, North shores Pipeline beach, the beach cove used in the movie rom Here to Eternity?with Burt and Deborah. Who needs a hotel pool with all that.I would stay at the Ilikai again any time. I understand it is now under new ownership. But, I have no complaints now.

<Author>emilyq
<Content>"pardon the inconvenience" ad nauseum Good:The rooms are quite large and quite a bargain. Though the building is ugly from the outside, the interiors are lovely with floor to ceiling windows and large balconies. Our room came with a full kitchen, and I believe that that is the layout for most rooms in this building.Bad: This building is ineptly managed. There were pardon the inconvenience signs at the following locations:Up escalators leading from street to lobbyMain elevators. Keep in mind that this is a 25 story building with probably 50-60 units on each floor, so five working elevators wouldn't be enough anyway. I don't know how many were actually functional. Some of them stopped on every other floor on the way down, regardless of whether there was anyone waiting. I overheard full-time residents complaining that this has been a problem for THREE YEARS. Bathers' Elevator (completely out of service). In theory this is the elevator you take if you are in a wet bathing suit, carrying a surfboard, or traveling with bicycle. Laundry room detergent dispenser (out of service)Dryer in laundry room (out of service)Only change machine in building for coin-op laundry (out of service)Also, there are large areas of this hotel that are just closed. Not out of service, but I guess run out of business. The restaurant, as well as most of the ground level shops. It has kind of a depressing feel. I was here for three weeks before I realized that there was a convenience store off of the lobby.Given all of these complaints, it says a lot about the rooms that I still gave this hotel three stars. It reflects what I value: quality of room at a good price. Also, the location was nice, in my view, because it is close to Waikiki without being in the middle of the craziness. Plus it makes the rest of Honolulu much more accessible.I can't comment on the hotel experience because I was not a hotel guest. Instead, I rented one of the condo units through an agent, Honey Jean Katsarsky, which was an entirely unpleasant experience starting the day after she cashed our check. Hotel guests, however, seemed fairly happy about the services they received, and I can vouch for the quality of the rooms.

<Content>Very spacious and well appointed room. I was going through places we had stayed and realized I had not written a review for this hotel. <Author>Walt_M_H
<Content>Still Ups and Downs at the Ilikai Be prepared to be flexible at the Ilikai--keep expectations minimal and you will enjoy your stay. A few things to note - the elevators going down stop ridiculously at many unneeded floors- going up they are OK.The city view room I checked into had a broken air conditioning unit that was noisy and full of ice, dripping water down on the carpet near the bed....but the management quickly moved me to a room that was very clean, comfortable and with a quiet and efficient air conditioner. I am glad I just did not grin and bear it but piped up right away to complain.That first room would have totally ruined my stay.I did not receive housekeeping on any of the 4 days I was there.I had to call guest services for the house man to deliver toilet paper, towels, soap, coffee. He came right away but I felt I was being obligated to tip for these deliveries.This is a bit unusual if you ask me.There are several good restaurants nearby within 5 minutes for breakfast, lunch and dinner. The trolley services are free to go shopping and other tourist places.The concierge was not knowledgable or pretended not to be???... so be prepared to do your own investigating as to how to get places.I think this hotel should receive a 2 to 2.5 star rating. The room rates are affordable but the service is below my comfort zone. I am a fairly flexible person so it really didn't bother me. The room was clean but the service was aloof...more or less self-serve.Beautiful lobby, landmark 60's genre being updated - slowly.Construction still going on next door...from 7am to 5 pm.Balcony windows are good quality and keep 90% of the noise out.

<Author>cdame
<Content>An older property, but still beautiful inside - great value! We had a short vacation in Hawaii and after researching many hotels via Expedia, we chose the Ilikai as it was the most reasonably priced for having great views and being a five minute walk to the beach.a) Property is old from the outside, the turquoise color can go, but it looks very 70's. At one time, this was Waikiki's very first high-rise, but sadly, there are many new hotels around that physically outshine the Ilikai with their modernity. But don't judge this hotel by the way it looks.b) Front desk staff was nice...nothing outstanding, but service was quick and they were accomodating. Only snafu was that we paid via Expedia and wanted to upgrade when we arrived to a full kitchen (Expedia doesn't give a choice for this). They wouldn't accept the credit card that we planned to use for these expenses because it was in my maiden name and I updated my ID. c) I highly suggest using the Expedia concierge desk. Michael H. was very helpful in letting us know about local attractions, restaurants, etc...and they book right there.d) Getting out of the cab ($35 cab ride from airport, about 30 mins), we were impressed. The staff greeted us, the waterfalls/landscaping is quite nice, and there was an escalator to take us to the lobby. e) Elevators were slow and signs noted that they were being updated. I took the advice of a reviewer here and we used the bather's elevator most of the time - much faster. At times, the elevators were a bit ridiculous, many people waiting, stops on random floors, etc. But we just chuckled most of the time. We were on vacation and weren't going to stress about that.f) Thanksgiving night, the upscale restaurant on the top floor, Sarento's, had a lovely turkey/dressing dinner which was fabulous. Lovely views. The elevator going to the 30th floor is all window, great views yet again. Crab cakes we had as appetizer were fabulous.g) Ground were beautiful. Each night, the lanterns were lit along the courtyard, seemingly, by shirtless/shoeless young men in Hawaiian garb. It was cute. Friday nights, singers/dancers perform in the courtyard. Not too much activity going on since the other restaurants were closed, but it's just beautiful to see the courtyard from our room or sit in chairs and overlook the marina/ocean.h) Our room wasn't fancy, but just fine for what we needed. NIce showerhead, convenient kitchen, great view of the courtyard/marina/city/ocean. Most nights, we left the sliding door to the balcony open and let the cool breezes in. Kitchen wasn't super clean - microwave was filthy. We didn't use it. i) Many people complained about the lack of the restaurants in the hotel being closed - we were disapointed, but there were a few shops in the hotel including a general store (prices marked WAY up, box of Wal Mart Raisin bran was $6.99, so only if you REALLY need something. But Walgreens was a $7 cab ride away, so evened out). The HiIlton Hawaiian Village was a two minute walk next door and they have MANY shops and restaurants. I was very satisfied with this...only downer was that there was no room service. We would have liked to have had breakfast delivered to our room to eat on the balcony, but that's what the raisin bran was for!Overall, we had a good time and are pretty laid back, so we were very satisfied with the Ilikai and I would stay there again. It's a great value for being so close to the beach. There is renovation going on next door - we didn't her anything, but that made our walk to the beach longer - we couldn't cut through the lagoon they are building w/the Hilton - so instead of 2 minutes, five minutes to the main beach. No big deal.

<Content>The Ilikai has gone downhill... After my recent stay at the Ilikai, I have to say that I would second guess any inkling I might have to stay there in the future. That is most unfortunate, as my family and I have many fond memories of staying at the Ilikai in years past, and we really looked forward to our most recent stay. From the elevators being broken (the buttons didn't even work on the 25th floor), to the escalator being inoperable, to the ice machines on multiple floors malfunctioning, to the lack of communication among staff members, the stay was filled with frustrations and disappointments. In addition to that, upon check out, the front desk staff member who checked me out didn't even thank me for staying at the Ilikai! I have to say that had the front desk staff member been even mildly pleasant to me, it would have smoothed over some of the rougher spots of the trip to your hotel, but she didn't even have the courtesy or decency to thank me for my business. I am truly appalled at the lack of service that I received while at the deluxe ocean front hotel (per the website). It's pathetic for me to state that the best service that I received while at the Ilikai was from the valet. The new owner (changed hands a year ago) and Management needs to make some changes, as the website lays claim that the Ilikai has, extensive upscale accommodations and friendly, professional staff to provide impeccable service to meet your vacation needs. I saw/experienced neither of those claims. That's fraud in my eyes. It was sad to see the Ilikai in such disrepair, and upsetting that the employees treated me with such disrespect.

<Author>smalltowntexas
<Content>Beautiful hotel As soon as we checked into the hotel, we sat down with the concierge who happened to work with Expedia, Carlo. He was so helpful and booked all the tours we wanted with him. He is not at the likai every day so be sure to ask for him.Our room was to be a cityview, but were upgraded to a marina view with a kitchenette. The room was very nice and the bed was heavenly! Yes, the elevator could be slow if the hotel was very busy, but we did not have much of a problem. There is also an elevator for bathers and we took that at times since it seemed to be faster.The hotel was not as congested as many of the others which was relaxing. In my opinion, it was just as beautiful a hotel as the better known hotels in the area. All the tour companies picked up at the likai. Everyone was very friendly and helpful.On the downside, the escalator outside was not working and you had to climb stairs to the lobby which was a problem if you have bad knees. We wanted to have drinks on the lovely patio area in back of the hotel and watch the sunset but their restaurant was closed for renovation and no drinks were to be had.The trip to the beach was also a problem. Because there was renovations being done to the hotel next door, walking to the beach was long and not very nice having to dodge construction and car traffic.

<Author>BoopBooGirl
<Content>Best for the Price and Location After reading reviews of the Ilikai and figuring out that it would be highly likely that I get the Ilikai via Hotwire...I went for it. Upon late night arrival, I was pleasantly surprised. The hotel has been totally remodeled and looks wonderful. It is clean and the staff is friendly as well as accommodating. I asked to have a water view if possible (even though I knew we prepaid for a less desirable view via hotwire) and they upgraded our room to a suite with full kitchenette and view of the marina. The room was better suited for us because we were traveling with our two small children. Our girls slept on the sofa bed while we slept in what felt like one of those heavenly beds at the higher-end hotels. Needless to say we slept well.The room was large and very clean (which is hard to find these days). The lanai was huge. I discovered Bath  Body Works soaps  lotions in the bathroom which I loved. I don't think you will find a better place on the water for the money. The property is situated with part of the hotel facing the marina and the other half faces the sandy beach. We could have spent anywhere from $170 to $225 on up for a fancier hotel (and not necessarily on the beach) but I doubt we would have had a nicer time. Our room was only $106 per night! Would I return--absolutely!

<Author>kerryjaneNewMexico
<Content>Quiet and charming We really loved this hotel because it was quiet and charming. I traveled with my husband and 9 year old and we all loved the beds, the roominess of our two room suite and the city and ocean views from the 23rd floor. The lobby and rooms were clean, the staff friendly and efficient. <Author>Magnus-Maximus
<Content>Ideal for what we needed I always use Trip Advisor before booking any hotel so I was a little apprehensive about staying at the Ilikai after reading previous reviews. I'm happy to report that we did not experience any of the problems that previous reviewers have encountered. We took the airport shuttle to the hotel - $9.00 per person - it made a few stops before reaching our hotel but you can't beat the price! We arrived late at night so there were only a few passengers, during peak season this could get really busy though. I'm glad we didn't immediately rent a car as we were told that parking at the hotel has been increased to $50.00 per day (ouch!)The hotel gives a great first impression - waterfalls and sculptures in the lobby. Very nice. Valets are available to help with luggage; there are stairs to climb to the lobby (or you can use the escalator but it's hard with luggage). The receptionist was nice, not overly friendly but it was 11.30pm and we weren't feeling chipper either. We requested a late 2pm check-out time instead of 11am - not a problem.The room was larger than expected with a king size bed, sofa, kitchenette, large bathroom, all obviously recently renovated. The granite countertops are beautiful. Also in the room is an iron, ironing board, hairdryer and safe. We were very high up, the views are outstanding, we sat outside on the balcony many times. It is very, very noisy out on the balcony but you can't hear anything inside with the door shut - sleeping was no problem. The balconies have a table and chairs. The kitchen is adequately stocked with basic utensils and comes with a microwave, oven, full-size fridge, large sink area, coffee machine etc. Ok for two people, fine for a family of four with younger children, perhaps anymore would be too crowded. The bathroom has Bath and Bodyworks products - a nice touch - the only problem with the bathroom is how close the toilet is to the shower. Very strange! The bed was very, very comfortable. And great bedding!! The pillows are so awesome that I tracked down the company that makes them and purchased a couple of king size for my home. The best pillows I've ever used :-)We did not use the pool so I cannot comment on that only to say it looks very small and disappointing.There is a glass elevator up to the restaurant on top of the hotel. We didn't eat at the restaurant but went up and down the elevator several times - fantastic views.Tip: If you arrive late, as we did, and wake up jetlagged, disorientated and hungry there is a Starbucks conveniently located nextdoor. We needed the caffeine boost!The Ilikai is in a great location for all attractions, we walked everywhere. Although there is construction going on around the hotel we were not affected in at all and I would definitely stay here again.

<Author>GgirlHawaii
<Content>Awesome View for the Price We booked our hotel thru a condo website. We were not disappointed. Yes, this hotel needs to be updated but for the price we paid, we couldn't have gotten a better view. Our view from the 6th floor Yacht Harbor was outstanding. No buildings, no construction, sunset view and quiet. Are you kidding? It was too quiet at night. We stayed here before and sort of missed the weekend when more tourists would come and hang out at the pool. There are two pools. One is being remodeled as that part of the property has been sold, we heard to a company that will be renovating it to a 4 star hotel. The other pool is right in the middle of the hotel and Hilton. The construction on the lagoon will be done by September according to the workers we asked. But if you stay at the yacht side, you won't even know there's a construction going on. We were there for 11 days, elevators weren't a problem except for 2x. That's 2x in 11 days in a building with 25 floors. To tell you the truth, we were anticipating delays due from the reviews here but it wasn't that way at all. The kitchen is fully equipped. The staff is very friendly and helpful. Yes, I'd stay here again.

<Author>bcpaula
<Content>Downhill Slide For The Ilikai I would think twice before booking a trip at the Ilikai Hotel in Waikiki. I stayed here on business 5 years ago and the place has gone downhill since then. The elevators don't work every time. Even if you are supposed to go down to the lobby area, they sometimes go up to the 24th floor. At first, I thought I had too many Mai-Tais, but other guests were making similar complaints. There is a sign next to the elevators saying that they are renovating, but I don't see any work being done on them. My room's refigerator doesn't work and it looks like that has been the case for some time. The knobs on the a/c unit are missing, so I cannot adjust the temperature or fan level and the iron's control knob is missing as well. Almost forgot-the ice machine on my floor is broke so I had to use the stairs to get some ice!To be fair, the staff has been very polite and helpful, but the maintenance and quality control is really lacking here. They should spend less time and effort keeping the lobby area immaculate (it is very clean and beautiful) and more time fixing all of the little problems that add up to unhappy guests. They don't even have a restaurant that serves breakfast or lunch in the hotel. Hotwire.com rates this 3 and a half stars-NO WAY! There have to be other hotels at a similar price that you can stay at instead of here. I booked the Prince hotel last year for $30 more a night-what a difference!!! Unless I hear from other travelers in the future that the Ilikai has done a huge transfomation, I would never stay here againButch PaulaPleasant Hill, CA

<Content>Ilikai Hotel The Ilikai Hotel is a good place to sleep at. I don't smoke but thought I would let smokers know! I know this because there were smokers in our group. Also, the Hilton next door is doing some construction and the workers start work around 6 A.M. every morning.

<Author>amrkitty
<Content>Could have been so good! This is a beautiful hotel in a convenient location. The problems I had were the same other people have mentioned before:1. Ask if there is a convention being held at the hotel while you are there. The Yoga people made our entire stay difficult. I guess since they had been there longer they felt as though they ran the place. I overheard one of them say they were to be there 9 weeks (?) 2. The elevators are RIDICULOUS! When they are working, the go up and down erratically within the same trip, shake, squeak, stop at every floor, and Yoga people have learned that the only way to get where you need to go is to cram into the one working elevator that services 25 floors. Nothing like having sweaty sportswear against you in the elevator...3. You will most likely not get the room you requested. I realize this is not guaranteed when you book, but come on, I asked for a double room. I was angry to be paying this much to sleep on a fold-out couch. 4. They advertise that there is a car rental on site. There is, but they have a VERY small fleet, are open only until 1 pm, and you have to return the car to a different location. Extremely inconvenient. The upsides are:1. Location is good. You are on the quiet end of Waikiki Beach, but if you want to go where the action is, it's a short walk. 2. The snorkeling is great in the morning; only about a five minute walk from the start of the beach. Go down in front of Fort DeRussy park, straight out from the volleyball courts and Lifeguard station T1. About 30 feet in from the buoys you will find a cleaning station where fish hang out and wait to get the junk picked off of them by other fish. The only problem is it starts to get murky after about noon. 3. There is a convenience store inside the hotel where you can buy (relatively) inexpensive things for lunch and breakfast. There is fruit, yogurt, muffins, granola bars, frozen stuff, etc. that you can get if you don't want to spend the time and money eating in their restaurants.

<Author>wwwench
<Content>great location  My husband and I just returned from a week at the Ilikai and liked many things about this hotel. However, the Ilikai has serious problems that urgently need to be addressed. Until I'm sure that substantive changes have been made, I will not be back.We stayed in a deluxe room with a balcony on the 23rd floor. The views of the harbor, park and city were drop-dead gorgeous and we spent many happy evenings on the balcony, toasting the sunset. Our room was large and lovely--not fancy, but comfortable and well-decorated--with two big closets (not enough hangers, but housekeeping brought more on request), two refrigerators, plug-and-play Internet, separate bath and shower, OK toiletries, abundant fluffy towels, and a comfortable bed with bountiful pillows and quality linens. (There were no bathrobes and no minibar, which seemed odd at this price point.) Light control was good and the air conditioner worked perfectly. We slept extremely well in this room.I loved the location of the Ilikai, a bit off the beaten track, overlooking the Yacht Club, a short walk to Waikiki beach on the east and Ala Moana Park on the west. At this wonderful park (conveniently located across the street from Neiman Marcus!) you can walk, run, bike, swim, surf, roller-blade, play tennis, picnic or just bask in the sun, along with real Hawaiians in their glorious diversity. I also loved Canoe's, the little restaurant off the lobby, overlooking the harbor. My husband being otherwise occupied by meetings in windowless rooms, I discovered the bar there--a convenient place with excellent food and a friendly staff, ideal for lunching alone. The staff was genuinely excellent. Valet parkers were speedy. The front desk was friendly and efficient. The concierge got us reservations, at the very last minute, at every restaurant in which we wanted to eat. Plus, when my hair needed emergency attention, she sent me to the Paul Brown Salon, where I got one of the best color-cuts of my life (by Toru Yamamoto--worth a trip to Hawaii!). Housekeeping came promptly when called (I always requested an early morning cleaning during my walk) and left everything spotless. Room service (from Canoe's) was glacially slow (an understaffing problem, we learned) but once the nice waiter arrived, the food was delicious. And the bartenders and waitstaff at both Canoe's and Sarento's (the expensive, top-floor restaurant, with fabulous views) were letter perfect. The only bad staffing area was the bell desk: at check-in, we were never able to get anyone to help us with our luggage, even after repeated calls. Bellmen were assisting other customers--forever! When we finally gave up and decided to carry our own bags, we couldn't even get a luggage cart. We ended up dragging and hauling everything by hand. Which seemed to be par for the course at the Ilikai, where I seldom saw a bellman and observed many guests schlepping their own bags.A more serious problem was the elevators, some of which were totally inoperable, none of which functioned properly. The beach elevator was completely dead during our stay. Ergo, the regular elevators were packed with people in wet bathing suits and sweat-soaked athletic clothes. The elevators either stopped at every floor or zoomed past the floors selected, to the dismay of the grouchy guests. Sometimes, when you got into the elevator, it wouldn't move at all. At other times, the doors would open and the elevator car would be ominously dark. The fan was broken in the elevator to the top floor restaurant, Sarento's--a glass elevator on the outside of a building in a torrid city, with no ventilation?! I got in anyway, but by the time I arrived at Sarento's, was literally drenched in sweat. This was not just an inconvenience, but a health hazard. There were no elevator repairmen on the scene, not ever, just signs on the elevators apologizing for the inconvenience (which, we learned from the long-term residents, has been going on since February!). Compare and contrast: when I stayed at the Four Seasons in Las Vegas in January and one of the elevators went down, there was a repair crew there within hours and the elevator was back on line the next morning. At the risk of sounding like a spoiled little princess: where I come from, functioning elevators in high-rise hotels are not just optional amenities, like bathrobes or minibars, but necessities. Getting them in working order is part of the cost of doing business, and if the Ilikai management cannot afford to repair the elevators, they should get out of the way and sell the hotel to somebody who can. Also, we learned one night when we ordered room service that most of the wine choices were not available because Canoe's restaurant was closing that Friday and nothing was being restocked. When I asked the bartender about this, he confirmed that management was closing Canoe's because, according to them, it didn't make enough profit. Also, they were redecorating. In the bartender's opinion, this was a ruse by management to replace long-time, unionized employees with cheap labor. The workers were invited to reapply for their old jobs if/when the restaurant reopened, but nobody I talked to expected to be rehired. If the sight of long-time coworkers (many of whom had worked there for 20-plus years) crying in each other's arms is not enough to ruin your trip to Honolulu (and inspire you to avoid the Ilikai like the plague!) how about the prospect of no casual, reasonably-priced restaurant in the hotel to have a drink or lunch? And what about room service? I didn't notice anyone hurrying to replace our old room service menus (from Canoe's) with new menus from Sarento's (currently open only for dinner) or the other restaurant in the hotel, Tanaka of Tokyo, which is quite expensive.Worst of all, the fire alarms malfunctioned. On our last night in the hotel, at about 3:45 a.m., the fire alarm sounded, and a voice (in English) told us to not to worry, but to wait for further instructions. Which worried me. (Isn't this what they initially told the guests during the MGM Grand fire?!) I got dressed and went out onto the balcony to see if I could spell smoke or hear the fire trucks coming. No on both counts. But I could see a flashing blue light in the lobby of Sarento's, the rooftop restaurant. Ten minutes later, I saw the glass elevator go up. Which also worried me. Shouldn't the elevators be off during a fire alarm?! Then, another voice (in Japanese) came on the emergency broadcast system and said...um, I don't know what it said, since I don't speak Japanese. My husband and I decided not to wait any longer, hightailed it down the hall, found the emergency exit (there were no safety lights in the dark alcove between the exit door and the door to the stairwell), and walked down 23 flights of to the lobby--where we were greeted by a harried security guard, who said there was no fire and we should go back upstairs. Which is when we learned from one of the condo owners that the fire alarms have been malfunctioning for months and have not been repaired by management--and that, because of all the false alarms, the Honolulu Fire Department will not come to the Ilikai unless someone (presumably, the harried security guard) calls them on the phone and confirms that there really is a fire. (So, if that person is burned to a crisp, or passed out from smoke inhalation, the fire department never comes at all?!) Call me a worry wart, but I see this as serious safety issue which, during a real fire, could cost people their lives. And with so many lodging choices in Honolulu, why would anyone stay in a hotel that shows such callous disregard for the safety of their guests by cheaping out on the fire alarms? Plus, if management hasn't been maintaining something as important as the fire alarms, what else have they also been neglecting? The electrical wiring? The fire sprinkler system?

<Author>akimi
<Content>going downhill fast The Ilikai gets worse and worse with every visit. There is no more buffet breakfast, just an overpriced although tasty menu.If you have stayed there before, be advised, there is no more large pool and there is lots of construction on the Hilton side. The little coffee shop has been consolidated with the small market. All the nice little touches are disappearing. The elevators are often out of order. The Ilikai is definitely transitioning towards condos and residents, with fewer amenities for the visitor. The escalator was out of order the whole time we were there. Of course it still is convenient to walk to Ala Moana with lots of great shopping and restaurants there. As long as you're not expecting the old Ilikai or paying a high rate, this is an OK place to stay.

A lot of these suites are privately owned and many have been upgraded such as this one.

<Author>BobtheWestie
<Content>Old, Sold, and it shows My wife and I in one room, and our 2 adult children in another, stayed at the Ilikai for 2 weeks. We were extremely disappointed with the state of this once grand hotel. There are older hotels in Waikiki, but they are much better maintained than the Ilikai.Half of the hotel's facilities are vacant, under construction, or have been sold, including the larger of the 2 swimming pools and the entertainment zone for younger guests.This is our first stay at the hotel, but not our first visit, having lived in and around Honolulu for 12 years since 1967. We visited many friends who stayed at the Ilikai over the years. We also occasionally took visitors to the Top of the I, but it wasn't easy to get to on this trip because of the sad state of the lifts.I do have to admit that the rooms are some of the most comfortable that I have experienced. But, as is often stated, you don't go to Hawaii to stay in your room.The hotel is only about a 10 minute walk from Ala Moana Shopping Center, but is about 20 to 30 minutes from the main Waikiki shops, beach, and entertainment district. Unless the room, itself, is your main conern, stay at one of the many Waikiki hotels. You can always catch The Bus to Ala Moana.

<Author>SydneySusy
<Content>Comfortable  Stayed there last week for 5 nts all up in Ilikai tower - 4 in a city view room, and 1 in an ocean view room. City view room has some road traffic noise with windows open, but nothing an average sleeper would worry about. The fridge was actually noisier! The rooms are just like the website- modern, very comfy (great bed) and have all you need incl kitchen, internet access, sofa, a/c. Would have rated our experience excellent except for the slow lifts - only 3 in service, others being refurbished. I'm very fussy when it comes to hotel rooms and Ilikai was excellent value in that regard.Location is great if you want to be away from the main hubbub of Waikiki but within short walk to Waikiki beach (via Hilton) or Ala Moana Shopping centre. Lots of eateries within 2 min walk. We parked out the back at the marina ($1 for 4hrs) one night but went the valet parking the other nights ($20/day) as it was easier. There's also a garage round the corner for $14/day, but you don't need a car if you're only staying in Honolulu as buses stop right out front, traffic an be pretty bad and parking downtown just costs more$$.

<Author>nocturnalgirl72
<Content>A work in progress Part of this hotel is a timeshare (Shell Vacations) and part is a regular hotel. Used to be the Renaissance now I think it is owned by Marriot. We had a timeshare room for 5 nights and a regular hotel room for the kids for the other 5 nights. The big annoyance at this hotel that affects everyone is the lack of working elevators. Extremely irritating to have to deal with 25 floors and having to wait forever for an elevator. Only 2 or 3 out of the 5 or 6 worked as the others were being renovated. The hotel was hot and muggy too due to the lobby being exposed to the outside but thank god the rooms had A/C. The Shell Vacations check in desk in inconveniently located across the courtyard, downstairs, and of course the escalators didn't work either. Also, only one pool was open as the other was closed. This hotel is located right next to HHV and their beach was only a few minutes walk. The rooms were nice and roomy. The timeshare room had a double bed, and a pull out sofa sleeper and a full kichen, and balcony. Big spacious bathroom, and TV with a ton of cable channels. Regular hotel rooms city view only had a king bed so one of the kids had to sleep on the floor. Plenty of room though. They wanted 60.00 a night to upgrade to ocean view/2 doubles and we were already paying $160/night. Parking is a pain and expensive. Across the street is a parking garage and its $14/day. There is free parking at the marina if you can find it but free parking in HNL is VERY hard to find so plan on paying for less frustration. In the hotel room, the A/C leaked and dripped water on some legal documents. Since the evidence was already on a plane I had to fight tooth and nail for a $25 credit which they finally gave to me. This hotel overall was a decent stay, but the East side of Waikiki (Kalakaua Ave) by the zoo was a better location this one and next time I would rather stay at the other end of Waikiki. Still this was a good location. Due to the lack of working elevators, escalators, and one closed pool, this is not a 4 star hotel but a 3. There are nicer hotels in Waikiki but then this one was not a dump either.

<Author>AlohaBoundVancouver
<Content>Dissapointed With The Changes At The Ilikai I have to whole heartedly agree with the review I just read about the state of the Ilikai Hotel. I have stayed there on every trip I have taken to Hawaii in the last 15 years and was sadly disappointed on this trip. My husband and I were there in May 2006 and had a great time, access to all of the pools and facilities, service at the pool (both food and drink), and great staff. Sadly, only 8 months later the story was very different when we returned in January 2007. Only two of the elevators worked the whole time we were there, and even then you were a little nervous to use them!! There was little if any food and drink service at the one remaining pool, where most of the seats were reseved long before anyone was at the pool and would stay reserved until someone would arrive to occupy them late afternoon when the sun crept around. Even though there was a sign posted that chairs could not be saved for more than 15 minutes, I guess if you tipped the pool attendent enough the rules could go out the window. Canoes restaurant got rid of their buffet that you used to have for breakfast every morning and even the smoothies that they serve for breakfast had changed in preparation and were not the same. The staff just does not seem to care anymore. Its unfortunate that this once grand hotel has been reduced to nothing more than a shell of its former self. Next trip we are planning to stay at the Hilton Hawaiian Village as their reputation is second to none and we will unfortunately not return to the Ilikai again.

<Author>Freq_Travel_guy
<Content>This is not the Ilikai we used to love!!! I've stayed at the Ilikai for over 20 years. Recently, it was a Marriott hotel chain, but they sold it and it is now independently owned. I'm sad to say, the hotel is a disaster. I'm not been dramatic -- everything that could go wrong in an hotel is happening in the Ilikai. The basic infrastructure is failing. For over two weeks, only 2 or 3 our of 6 elevators are working. The wait time can be up to 30 minutes to get downstairs. They have shut down and sold one of two pools to another company so the entire hotel is forced to share one small pool along with the condo association which has units in the building. They are mostly retired snow-birds who get down to the pool first thing in the morning, reserve their chairs and then disappear. On three different occasions we could not get a seat around this small pool, and there wasn't a single server offering drinks. While we did eat at the outdoor restaurant Canoe, we were startled by the rat that was snacking under our table. Yes, you read that right... it was a rat. The room cleaning has become sub-par as they have cut back almost 50 percent on the cleaning staff. Our room often wasn't cleaned until after four in the afternoon, and then it was often still filthy. The quality and quantity of the staff is deplorable. They joke about the state of the hotel and say they are the last of the Mohicans... they know the writing is on the wall. I have a history in this hotel and it breaks my heart to see it deterioate in such a way. Bu sadly, at these prices, I advise you to stay away.

<Author>Ted_Fez
<Content>Ilikai Pretty Reliable I have stayed at the Ilikai nine or ten times over the past six years. I frequently travel to Honolulu on business and typically choose from a half-dozen or so hotels. The Ilikai is located at the west end of Waikiki, about a 5-10 minute walk from Hilton Hawaiian Village. It is in a good location for me because my office is near the airport and I can avoid all the traffic of Waikiki.The Ilikai tends to be pretty reliably good value. It is not overly fancy and faces a marina (as opposed to beach), but one can get a nice marina/ocean view. The staff are friendly and the rooms are usually pretty nice. The hotel went through a renovation a few years ago with fairly good results. There is a nice workout room on the second floor for those that want to exercise. Canoe's Restaurant on the ground floor is an indoor/outdoor restaurant which is particularly pleasant for breakfast. There is a very nice retaurant (Sarrento's) with a fabulous view on the top floor for special occasions. There are also modestly priced restaurants within walking distance. I would recommend the hotel for just about anyone except those that want to be right on the beach or in the thickest part of the Waikiki scene.

<Author>julietravel
<Content>Excellent service Excellent service from the Ilikai. The valets were quick and very friendly. The concierge set up our room with food and drinks waiting for us upon arrival and nice notes for each of us. The rooms are very clean and spacious. Beds were really comfortable with a feather top and pillows to match. The bell hop was waiting at our door with our luggage before we got to our room and filled our ice bucket before he left. Anytime we called for something (extra towels, etc.) it was brought up to us quickly. The sunsets are beautiful overlooking the yacht harbor. This is a nice, quiet end to your evening. We took our 2 kids, 10 and 12, and would walk the beach after dinner to the other areas with music and shows. The Ilikai is at the beginning of Waikiki and very easy to get to if you have a rental car. We had a convertible and the valet would have the top down for us and ready to go. We had an ocean view room with a kitchen. The housekeeping would even do our dishes each day. The construction going on at the Hilton didn't have any effects on our stay. The Ilikai is a very nice, clean, well maintained hotel with an excellent staff. It's close to everything like Ala Moana Shopping Center (and park), Kalakaua Avenue (all the shops, entertainment, etc.) and a 3-5 minute walk around the lagoon to the beach. It was just nice in the evening to sit outside overlooking the pier and watching the sunset without all the hustle and bustle going on at some of the other hotels. (You're not far from all the hotels down the beach with live music). We have stayed there 3 times and have always enjoyed our stay.

<Author>Erica-SantaCruz
<Content>Be advised, the Ilikai Hotel wasn't that great. We stayed at the Ilikai Hotel in Waikiki for 5 days and found it through a property manager. We had read reviews of it on Trip Advisor prior to our trip and knew it was a mixed bag. Initially, we had thought we were staying at the Ilikai Marina, which is two buildings away. The Ilikai Hotel had good points and bad points. The unit was beautifully remodeled with nice attention to detail. The bed, pillows, and linens were very clean and comfortable and pleasing to the eye. The lobby was very nice and comfortable also.On the negative side, the unit, and likely all the units in the Ilikai Hotel were very noisy. Each unit has its own AC unit and the noise is loud and constant. It was impossible to sleep with the sliding glass door open to get fresh island air due to the hundred other AC units going all night long. With the sliding glass doors closed and our AC unit on, it was also too loud.Even though our unit was called a one bedroom, it actually was a studio, which is common in Hawaii. There was no wall between the bed and the living room; it was just one room. If two couples were staying there or if people had kids, everyone would be in the same room. We could also hear the refridgerator running all night long as well.The view is an ocean view, but it was obstructed by buildings on either side, so it wasn't a full ocean view. Our unit was overlooking a huge construction site at the Hilton Hawaiian Village. All we could hear all day long was the beep, beep, beep of heavy equipment backing up.Knowing what I know now, I would not stay at the Ilikai Hotel again. Having checked things out around there, I would definitely stay at the Ilikai Marina (across the footbridge) in an oceanview condo. That building has unobstructed ocean views, central AC, and is away from the construction site. It seemed a lot quieter and nicer.Hope this helps someone.

<Content>Happy with Ilikai Stayed here on my first visit to Hawaii with my wife. I went to the Hilton to use their biz center.It is a 5 minute walk aroung the lagoon to the Hilton beach, but there is lots of free parking out back near the marina.Everything is a $6 cab ride away. Or you can walk the 20-30 minutes.Did not try lunch or breakfast there.I was happy with the Ilikai and would not hesitate to return.

<Author>mjgriffy
<Content>Calculated Compromise Formerly a Renaissance Hotel, formerly a condo, formerly a timeshare?The Illikai is also a condo/hotel/owner occp/multi-use property. In my opinion, it is not in the center of Waikiki as it is closer to Ala Moana and the Hilton Hawaiian Village. To some, that may be a bonus. But to me (a walking shopping beachgoer) it is a too far from everything else. The building itself is in fine repair, but the condition of each unit will depend on from whom you are renting (time share, condo, hotel, etc). With nice pool deck and bars overlooking a marina and the Hilton, the room views can be great or average (and noisy) depending on which way you face. Most units are kitchen or kitchenette. I recommend upgrading to a higher level ocean view room, but then you would get into several hundred $$ a night. Above $300/nt I would really recommend staying somewhere else. For pictures and location information go to their website ilikaihotel then Google to find better rates. As always; I travel to Waikiki several times a year, I can advise that Waikiki is a nice tropical urban adventure. The city comes with the negatives of a big city, along with the overwhelming benefits of a beautiful beachfront resort. Generally, everything in Waikiki is  little tired?although there have been continuous improvements in the last few years. If you are traveling solo, take Roberts Hawaii from the airport for $10 (no rsvr rqd).Two or more people, take a taxi from the airport to the hotel (should be under $30). In Waikiki, nearly everything is walking distance or a short shuttle/bus away. If you need a car for the day, you can rent one in Waikiki.

<Author>AA-Platinum
<Content>Not up to expectations irst things first....as of 12 July 2006, this is no longer a Renaissance hotel (the property was sold and the new owners are converting it to a Condo). As a result, no more Marriott Points. The flip side is that prices dropped by more than 1/3.Secondly, this hotel is way over rated, based on the comments from previous guests posted on Trip Advisor. My wife and I (along with our 5 month old) stayed here for a week in early July. In early April, we booked a Waikiki view room, but about a two weeks before we left, we were upgraded to an Ocean View. What we got was a view of a construction site (if you leaned out over the balcony, you could see the lagoon and ocean by the Hilton.The room itself was comfortable enough. We asked for, and were provided with acomplementary crib for the baby. We also requested and received a room with a kitchen, which was a real saver. However, as a result, there is minimal storage space. The bathroom was basic, with a shower stall rather than a shower/tub. The King-Size bed was comfortable, and there were plenty of pillows. Maid service was acceptable (although one day they never showed). We were supposed to have a newspaper delivered to our room daily (one of the local Honolulu ones). It came 3 days out of 7. There was good airflow so we had no need to use the air conditioner at night.There are two pools. One is small, the other smaller. It made it difficult to take the baby into the water since people were constantly on top of the baby.Our biggest complaint was that, although they knew that we had a baby with us (and hadrequested a quiet room), was that our room overlooked the construction site. The noise was so bad (and we were on a high floor) that my wife and the baby could not stay in the room during the day (I was at a conference).All-in-all, not a bad hotel, just not what we had hoped for.

<Author>b555
<Content>Upgrades are everything We spent my birthday week in May, 2006, at the Marriott Renaissance Ilikai. It goes by the name Ilikai locally to avoid confusion with the Marriott Waikiki Beach Hotel. A shuttle is easily available from the beautiful airport. Several insights to share. Checking in can be confusing as there are 2 entrances. The main one is gorgeous with flowing fountains. The side one (actually another hotel's lobby) is used by taxis and buses often and connects inside to the front desk. Huge confusing lobby. Ask for help. When checking in ask about upgrades (for additional cost from $20-$35 a night). Some wings face east (and the beach and fireworks on Friday night) and others face the sunset. Yours might face town. Some have kitchens (highly useful as meal prices are shocking). The kitchens are sparcely furnished so you may have to ask for items from housekeeping. The higher floors don't cost extra and the balconies are comfortably large. Buy the upgrade!! Cooking simple meals in the condo and using the balcony for cocktail hour is the greatest. Use the consierge desk for advice. They are very nice. Ask them for a local bus sheet. The fare is $2 and they go everywhere, even to the eastside beaches, palace, academy of arts, and Sea Life. It's kind of a slow ride, but interesting to see the local folks and neighborhoods. Drivers are helpful. We enjoued Germaine's laua and the bus was included. There are so many brochures, maps and tourist guides easily available that some bargains can be found. Pearl Harbor takes a couple of hours and is well worth the time. So is the submarine tour with headphones. These are reasonably priced. Follow these tips and you will have a great time with the wonderful Hawaiians at an affordable rate. Be aware that taxes added to every bill really add up. Look for bargains. Aloha.

<Content>DISGUSTING! - Honeymoon Gone Wrong Upon planning our honeymoon vacation with Fun Sun Vacations (who we don't recommend as well) we were under the impression that we would be placed in a simple yet pleasant suite at the Illikai, and we thought it would be a wonderful and unforgetable experience . When we arrived in Honolulu or more specifically in front of the Illikai we were met with great displeasure and rudeness by the door staff. One of the employees had picked up our bags out of the van that had dropped us off and threw them over to the side of the roadway in order to make room for the tourists who were in the cars to follow. It seemed as though they acted out in this manner towards all tourists who were unloading their things in front of the hotel. So we picked up our thrown belongings and struggled with tryng to load them onto the escalator in order to get to the lobby of the hotel. There were about three doormen who WATCHED us do this and not one of them was polite enough to offer us some help (even though this is a part of their job description). It being our honeymoon, we didn't allow this disgusting attitude to ruin our day untill we spoke with the front desk. It was here when we were informed that our lovely and yet very expensive ocean view suite (already paid for in advance) was located in the old grungy tower that didn't even face the ocean. Alright, so you may be wondering what's next? Well we opened the door to our crusty mold infested suite only to find TWO SINGLE BEDS!!!!! Now what are honeymooners supposed to think? My husband immediately went down to the front desk and complained. However his complaint was taken lightly and we were told that that was to be our room. The next day my husband approached the front desk several times with this issue, once again however staff at the Illikai displayed no sympathy. It wasn't untill I stormed up to the front desk and began shouting, screaming and swearing about our situation, then we were placed in a room that was somewhat decent and somewhat equivalent to the price that we payed. Did we get any money back --NO. Was there an apology of some sort -- NO. This hotel must have been the most disgusting and disgraceful hotel in terms of accomodations and staff. There was no sense of pleasing the customer, not one staff member was polite or helpful. It was overall a miserable place to be in paradise. Oh, by the way don't be fooled! They offer oceanview rooms but they really are not what they say. You can see the ocean if you turn at a large angle, but the majority of the view is of the neighbouring hotel (and you'll have to walk quite the distance to arrive at the nice part of the beach). If you're planning on having a peacefully relaxing time that may not happen due to the noise of the construction right next door. All around this was absolutely the most disgusting hotel we have ever been to!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location, would stay again! It was my mom's birthday, so we decided to splurge and take a trip to Hawaii to celebrate. The Ilikai was a great place to stay. Everytime we needed directions or any information, the staff was more than willing share their knowledge. It was close to everything! Instead of renting a car (the cost for parking anywhere in the area is insane!) we decided to take the Pink Line trolly up and down Waikiki or the bus. Both stops were very close to the hotel. The Ala Moana shopping center was a very quick walk (approx. 10 min) or just 2 bus stops away. The International Market was about a 20 min walk in the other direction. There's few places to eat on both sides of the hotel so everything was easily accessible. I would definately recommend staying here!

<Author>Relax4Life
<Content>Friendly Staff but doesn't live up to Renaissance brand of hotels I stayed at the Ilikai for a business trip.Positives:- Location is very good to get to most of the businesses located in town- Close to the Ala Moana Mall across the street- Most rooms have some view of the water without paying extra money- Balcony is a nice touch, but probably doesn't work well for most rooms (see below)- Down Comforters- Lots of kids (Good for families, not couples)- Very friendly staffNegatives:- Decor looks totally outdated, Needs a major facelift! You may be frightened when you first arrive because it looks more like an apartment building than a major hotel chain. Do NOT believe the deceiving pictures on the hotel website!!! That's where I went wrong.- The balcony on most rooms in the main hotel look into other hotel rooms- so if you expect to sit in your balcony without having someone possibly stare you down....NO luck here.- Not very good for office travel as there is no wireless internet- you only have direct access to the ethernet line which is a pain if you want to check email in the lobby, or near the pool.- Pools are crowded and small- Food is mediocre- but okay because there are a ton of awesome places nearby- Gym looks like it is in a scary basementOverall assessment:If you are a business traveler, there are better options (Hawaiian Prince Hotel next door is excellent). For the vacationer, I would say you would be happier staying somewhere else further down in Waikiki which will be more central to the beautiful ocean and nightlife. This hotel is expensive and certainly does not invoke the luxury vacation feel. Unfortunately, I believe the Ilikai is stuck in an 80s time warp where teassed hair and garbage pail kids are in.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Lovely Hotel My Husband and I stayed here for our Honeymoon after Marrying in Las Vegas. We were lucky enough to swap to this hotel from our original choice of Outrigger Reef on the Beach Waikiki, as there was construction work near the outrigger. The outside of the Ilikai could do with a lick of paint, but as you walk up the stairs/Escalators you are faced with a beautiful Marble whale water feature. The lobby was open plan and nicely furnished, the staff were very helpful. We chose to upgrade our room to a suite in the ilikai tower on the 24th floor, views out into the harbour and the mountains in the distance. In the at sunset they would hold a touch lighting ceremony and some evenings have a band playingby the pool. This hotel was nice, quiet (not many children)but unfortunatley I found Waikiki to be very built up and commercialised but the Hawaiians were very welcoming and the weather great with lots to do. If your looking for a livley place then Waikiki is for you, however if you are looking for tranquility then try the North Shore of Oahu (where 'Lost' is filmed) or Maui.

<Content>Mama with 7 Month Old...Loved IT!!! I loved our stay at the Ilikai. I met my husband there while he was on travel for business. The room was great. I had my 7 month old and the staff was great. The maid service delivered a wonderful little crib (not a portable travel crib). It had a sheet over the matress and a matching blanket. I am very cautious about my baby laying in bedding that isn't mine but it smelled nice and clean and he loved sleeping in it. The room was large. It was large enough to have my suitcase and my son's suitcase out as well as a stroller and a backpack carrier. And he still had room to crawl around. We had a kitchen in ours. Full fridge, sink, microwave and stove. We didn't cook but it was nice to have the micorwave and the fridge for the baby bottles and water bottles. The bathroom was large and I liked not having a tub and just a shower, it was a nice change.We like walking so we walked to the shopping center a couple of times and also down to the main part of Waikiki three times. I enjoyed the poolside entertainment at night and the atmosphere during the day. We ate at the Japanese resturant and it was real good. They were great with my son. We also had a couple of younger kids at the table and the chef catered alot to the younger ones. We had lunch at the Canoes and that was very good. We sat out in the patio seating and enjoyed the view. We found a lot of resturants near by and didn't need to look far for food.My used my stroller alot around the grounds of the hotel and everyone was very friendly and helpful with any questions or needs that I required for my son. I loved it.We stayed 5 days 4 nights and it was great. I did spend a lot of time in the room with no car and a 7 month old that needed naps and I enjoyed it!

<Content>Hotel vs. Condos: There's a Difference There's an important distinction here: the Ilikai is two properties in one-- the Renaissance Ilikai Waikiki Hotel and the Ilikai Waikiki Condos. They are actually different units in the same property, but managed separately.I stayed at the Renaissance Ilikai Waikiki Hotel property for 4 nights, 5 days recently and loved it. The rooms are freshly redone, very clean, and well-appointed.I can't speak for the condos, but the hotel was super. Renaissance is a higher-end Marriott brand and demands a fairly high standard. I'd stay at this hotel again any day!

<Content>mixed reviews, mixed feelings Work booked me into one of those vacation club condos in the Hotel Ilikai. I read the mixed reviews on this website with some concern (was tempted to change my booking). Although its a 15 minute walk from downtown Waikiki, it is also only 10 minutes from the interesting Ala Moana Shopping Centre and 15 from the sensational Hawaiian Convention Centre. The hotel has plenty of shops to choose from too so I did alot of my souvenier shopping there and saved time from all the 'cheapskate' pennypenching like the other tourists do. So go visit the Renaissance and enjoy your Hawaiian getaway, I did!!

<Author>SEAluvzHNL
<Content>Disappointed, but made the best of it! I booked this hotel through Hotwire. The price was excellent, and being a return guest from years prior, I knew the property well. When we pulled up to the hotel, we were greeted with a new, beautiful lobby. (They've renovated since my last stay, and changed ownership, Nikko Hotel to Starwood Property) We were floored however when the bellman told us that both Valet  Self-Parking was $20/Day! What a rip off! I checked my family in (2adults,2children). When the front desk agent gave me directions to our room, I knew right off the bat that we were headed for the older rooms. Sure enough, I was right. I knew ahead what we were in for! I was so disappointed to the small room we entered. The bathroom was tiny and the tub/shower was gross! The caulking was molding and breaking away, the bath mat that goes in the tub had hairs from the previous guest (yuck!) The light was out too, and we had to call maintenence to replace the bulb. We had a view of Hobron St and The ABC Store (busy intersection). The noise was terrible, but luckily we didn't stay in our room all day! I went downstairs to talk with the front desk to see if we could switch rooms, and he was more than happy to for a $30/day upgrade to the Ilikai Tower. It would be the same room type, but with a King Bed, and facing more of the busy street in front. FYI, this is the same room type if you book through ClassicHawaii Vacations! (that just floors me!) I know for a fact that rooms inThe Ilikai Tower are higher up, nicer, bigger, and rooms have more amenities, and telling him that I was a Marriott Rewards Member, and stayed many times prior to this trip didn't get me in! So, disappointed, I went back to the room and just made it work! The main pool was nice, pool bar service was pricey, and if you didn't purchase anything from their bar menu, you couldn't eat it by the pool! You had to sit out of the area (out of sight!) How rude! I have 2small children and they are picky eaters! But for the rap I went through at check-in, I did what I needed to do to keep myself and my family happy! Plus, other guests approached us too and they got the same rap from the bar server too! They ignored them too!Overall, my advice, pay the higher price and get a nice room in the Ilikai Tower. It's worth it! I know! Don't expect the front desk staff to be nice and show aloha spirit with a free upgrade. (it was Aloha Week too, what a time to show it!) Being a local girl, I was ashamed!
