<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Book It Dano For those of you seeking advice on whether this property is worth staying at or not, let me put your mind at ease. I'm going to give you the bottom line....Go for it ! We stayed on the 22nd floor with a deluxe ocean view. The view was in fact deluxe, and the room was huge, as was the lani. Our room was spotless ( no mold, no spots on the carpet, no bugs and we didn't hear our neighbors next door ) All the pitfalls from the previous reviews were not to be found. Yes, the hotel is tucked away with a marina on one side, but there's a certain charm to that. The beach isn't that far away, just a 5 minute walk and you're right smack in the middle of where the Hilton Hawaiian folks hang out. And if you keep going another 10 minutes you'll find yourself in the quicksand of humanity known as Waikiki beach ( which is o.k if you're in to people watching, that's about all there's room for ).  We ate breakfast at Canoes resturant every morning cause it was part of the deal. The food was excellent, but a little expensive if it were to come out of my pocket. Yes, I know, the cost was tacked on to the room, but that went on the credit card. It left me with my wad to spend on other stuff. Parking is 20 bucks. I saw folks parking in the marina for free, but if you want convienience and security, spend the doe. In closing, just so you know, my opinion isn't skewed by romance, or clouded by a honeymoon, I was there with my daughter to see a USC game. The Ilikai would be great for all the aforementioned though. Couples in their 20's may want to go where there's more action. Oh, and visit the North shore. It's more tropical there. So if you were to ask the late Steve McGarrett of Hawii five 0 fame, I'm sure he'd tell you to BOOK IT DANO. Have fun!!!  
<Date>Sep 6, 2005

<Author>RutgersGuy
<Content>Save $$$ with private condo rooms The Ilikai is mixture of hotel rooms and private condos. We rented room 1108 from www.ilikai.com and were very satisfied with it. The price with taxes was about $150 a night, much less than the hotel rates. The room had a nice harbor view and was very comfortable. With the queen sofa open, it was cozy but perfect for a family of 4.We did not spend much time at the main part of the Waikiki strip, so the location was not an issue, but we found it convenient. The room was nicely furnished and included a well-furnished kitchen where Pat had left some treats for us in the fridge. The downside of renting a private condo is that you do not have access to hotel services. You don't actually check into the hotel so they don't know you're there. You have to carry your own bags and may not get to use the hotel's towels at the pool. I don't know who would help if there were a problem with the room. Pat, the rental agent, lives in the Ilikai and I think there's a condo management office. I was a bit nervous about prepaying for our whole stay without any info about the agent, but it turned out to be perfect for us.  
<Date>Sep 3, 2005

<Content>Horrible Experience--wouldn't recommend it I travel weekly, mostly for business--some pleasure. I chose the Renaissance Ilikai because it's a Marriott and I collect frequent traveler points. Most Marriott Hotels have upgraded their beds and they're great--another reason to stay at Marriotts. Overall, I've had great experiences with them.The Ilikai doesn't live up to any Marriott standard. It is an old hotel and our two-different rooms were very dated. The beds were old and uncomfortable. The furniture was dated--bamboo motif with plenty of wear. The carpets were soiled. The shower had mold on the walls and worst of all--long black hairs plastered to the shower walls from a previous guest. Also, there was not outlet to plug in my computer to work.The room we reserved was billed as Ocean View at $269 per night--what a joke! We were 10 floors above the street--the noise was deafening when we opened the window and you'd have had to hang out over the balcony to see the ocean (it was out there at the end of the street). We called and complained and next day they moved us down the hall. The room was exactly the same, but on the inside of the building, over the pool (also noisy). The carpets were soiled; bad bed, etc.! The last straw was waiting in line for a full 25 minutes to check out on the last day--two desk clerks were waiting on 25 or so people.The only exception was the food and service at Canoes Restaurant--it was superb. We ate in the restauant, had room service, and poolside--it was always great.

<Author>fand
<Content>Wouldn't stay there again I had an unfortunate problem at the Ilikai: my room was on the 4th floor directly overlooking the pool. The noise was so bad that I couldn't sleep. There were a lot of children screaming at the top of their lungs in the pool. I called the front desk, and the person who answered said that she would send security to ask them to quiet down. It didn't quiet down. 20 mins later, I called the front desk and asked them to send someone out there again, and she promised that she would. This time I looked out of my window down at the pool. NO ONE went up to anyone in that pool and asked them to quiet down. 15 mins later I called the front desk again and asked to be put in a quieter room. The woman informed me that security had taken care of the problem. She ignored my request for another room. I told her that I had been looking out my window and that security had not gone to the pool. She transferred me to a manager. I asked for a quieter room. She ignored my request and told me that she would call the pool attendant. I watched out of the window and the pool attendant did get a phone call and went over to the pool. Finally, by 11 pm or so, all of the kids were out of the pool and it was quiet enough to sleep. I travel all of the time for business, and I have never been treated so rudely as I was by the Ilikai staff. I will definitely not go there again. But, that said, my room was nice otherwise, and I really like the Canoes restaruant. I think that people may like this hotel, but ONLY if you get a room up in the tower away from the noise. One more thing...the walls are paper thin so you may be able to hear your neighbors quite well, and vice versa.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not typical renaissance quality Over the years I have stayed at many Marriott and Renaissance properties. This hotel did not meet the usual standards. There are just a few things that one should know before booking at this hotel. First, it is not on the beach. It is a short walk away. Also, the hotel is located at the far end of Waikiki, and is not in the center of where most activity takes place. However, it is next door to the Hilton Hawaiian Village, which provides entertainment. The rooms have recently been refurbished, and are nice, however the bathrooms still need much improvement. The shower/bathtub is extremely small, and did not appear well cleaned. The restaurants at the hotel are very good. The 2 pools are basic, and small, but pleasant and not overly crowded. Be aware that there is a significant amount of permanent residents, many elderly, living in the hotel full time. Overall, the hotel provided a fairly pleasant stay, but do not expect typical Marriott/Renaissance quality.

<Author>spookiedoodle
<Content>Had a wonderful stay here!! We spent 6 nights at the Renaissance Ilikai on Waikiki from January 6th thru 11th, 2005. I booked the room on Priceline and was surprised to get it for $60 per night. I was not expecting the top quality that we got with this room, due to the low, low price. Remember that January in Hawaii is HIGH season and you would expect to pay much more for a top notch room. The room was very large, in the Yacht Harbor Tower and was extremely comfortable and quiet. The only disappointment was the fact that we could not get a queen or king room - ended up with a room with 2 doubles, but it was non-smoking. Could have gotten a king smoking room, but prefer non-smoking. The hotel staff were extremely friendly and helpful. We needed to do a very late checkout because we had a 9:30PM flight back to the mainland. The charge for a 6PM checkout was an additional $50.00, but we thought it was well worth the cost. We had a convertible and did not want to drive all over Honolulu on our last day with a car full of luggage. This rate was called the Linger Longer rate and I would recommend it to anyone who needs a very late checkout. We truly enjoyed our stay at this lovely hotel and would highly recommend it to anyone!!!!

<Author>travelhappie
<Content>Great overnight stay... We were attending a wedding and stayed overnight in a kitchen with ocean view room on the 20th floor. Although the view was half blocked by one of the Hilton towers, it was stilll a nice view to wake up to. We had a King size bed plus sofa bed and a full kitchen with granite counters. There's a coffee maker with coffee and tea provided. The bed was very comfortable and we slept soundly. I'm sure a kitchen would come in handy for those wanting to cook breakfast in the room. The hotel is good for families who need the extra room. Although our bathroom only had a shower (not good for those little kids that need tubs). The staff was gracious and gave us a late checkout upon request. Newspaper left at door in the morning. It's only a few minutes walk to the Hilton property where you can enjoy their beautiful lobby. The only problem would be the large amount of elderly people who live there and stared at our loud children as if they were the devil himself. Also, the pools are small and plain. Overall, a good choice for the money, but not for the younger crowd who might want to be more in the center of Waikiki.

<Author>ChampagnePrincess
<Content>Wow, what a room! What a deal! Simply asked for a nice room at reception and just like that, we got a kitchenette room in the new tower, on the 3rd floor, facing the marina. It was gorgeous and huge. It had a full kitchen with an island and bar stools, a couch, lounge chair, king bed and sunset view. The patio was huge and came with a table and two chairs. We even got a newspaper each morning. Not bad for $69 a night through Priceline. We used our Entertainment Book and used several dinner coupons at the hotel's restaurants. Canoes was great - the best grilled ahi with lemon sauce I've ever had. Also ate right across the street at the pizza restaurant and enjoyed it. Don't go to Oahu without purchasing the Entertainment Book. We saved hundreds of dollars. The shows in Waikiki were real super savers. (Blue Hawaii Elvis show - savings $64) All meals - half price. Can't beat the deals. Lots of great shopping right downstairs in the hotel - so convenient. If you have kids they have special arcade deals that looked really reasonable. The pools were pretty small, but because of the high winds, we skipped them. The nightly torch lighting ceremony was nice, short and sweet. Make sure you take a jacket, at night it gets pretty chilly and windy. A short walk to the Hilton Hawaiin Village, should not be missed. It's so huge. Can't wait to get back to this hotel. Would recommend it to anyone. If your kids like McDonald's, it's right across the avenue, out the front door. Stay at this hotel - you'll love it. Also, it you get a chance, walk into the chapel, it's gorgeous.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A very reasonable hotel I spent five nights at the hotel in December 2004. The hotel is in a fairly neutral location in that it is at the extreme end of Waikiki beach, about five minutes walk from the actual sand. It is also at least 15 minutes walk from the main tourist shops in Kalakaua Avenue and 10 from the Convention Centre and Ala Moana Shopping Centre.I had an ocean view with a King size bed. <Content>Ok, but wouldn't stay again. We stayed at the Renaissance Ilikai Hotel as part of our honeymoon stay. We were there the week of November 1 and checking out November 5. First, I must say that the hotel is very hard to find and get to. We called for directions to the hotel 3 different times and finally were able to find it after looking for almost 45 minutes. I want to state that we booked this hotel on Hotwire at the rate of $92 per night, which I thought was a decent rate for Hawaii, and especially in the Wakiki area. The hotel staff was courteous upon arrival but they informed us that there would be a charge of $16 per night for parking. Kind of ridiculous since the hotel has been there since the 60's and the ramp is paid for by now. Anyways, we were upgraded to a room with a kitchen and refrigerator and stove. Upon entering the room, we realized that it was actually very nice. The decor was very up to date and it had Bath and Body ameneties which was nice. I read that they did a renovation to the hotel a short time ago so I was impressed. The thing I did not care for about this hotel was the location. It was in the Wakiki area but the nicer part of Wakiki is on down the road. The hotel didn't really sit on the beach and the part that it was on didn't have any people on the beach. So if you wanted to go to the part of Wakiki beach that had people surfing and so on, you needed to go down to the other part of the beach. If you are wanting a nice hotel in a great part of town I would definitely recommend the Sheraton Moana Surfrider hotel. It was an absolutely beautiful hotel that sat right on the beach. Also the Hyatt that was across the street from the Sheraton was also a nice hotel.

Saved quit a bit eating breakfast and most dinners in the room. Their is a Foodland in the shopping center at Ala Mona about 3 bloocks away. It has several small shops, a general store great for price about the same as larger stores great for getting drinks and small items for fridge. It has a short walkway that connects it Wikiki beach in front of the Hilton Village. Now Wikiki is crowded most times but for the feel of the beach it is nice, a park is there and a sidewalk that runs the entire length of the beach. Parking is bit higher than most places $16 a day but it is valet and your car is secure in a enclosed garage. The valets jhonny on the spot , helping with packages, giving directions. Fresh lays and flowers for your hair avaiable every day in the lobby help yourself. All the help very nice and helpful. The maid will even do the dishes in your room! The resturants all very good and priced right. The Harbor Pub across the street connected by a overpass walkway turned out to be our favorite. Best Pizza we ever had! Downtown is very walkable from the hotel with a lot to look at along the way.WOuld stay here again in a heart beat.  
<Date>Oct 12, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>How I Spent My Tax Return I loved the open-air lobby and the giant bouquets of tropical flowers located in the Renaissance Ilikai. The views--the ocean in front and Diamond Head to the left--was exquisit. The staff was very helpful, whether it was a change in room or simply asking for directions. Even though it isn't located directly on the beach, it is surrounded by a boat harbor and tide pool (smaller children may enjoy trying to catch the small schools of baby fish!). I didn't find the jaunt to the beach bad, especially since there is a walkway from the hotel leading directly to the beach. The room was very nice and clean, although the bed was extremely uncomfortable and the TV minute. Also, room service has limited hours which aren't condusive to tourists. The restaurants are nice and most tour buses pick up at the hotel for island sightseeing. The location is central to shopping, yet far enough away from the hubbub to still be able to sleep with the balcony doors open at night. All in all, a very good and memorable experience!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>More than a Few Steps to Waikiki Beach The Ilikai is isolated by a lagoon and fence from the other hotels on Waikiki beach. You have to walk quite a long distance to access the beach not a few steps as the hotel claims. Once you reach the nearest beachfront area, you won't be able to go into the ocean unless you're wearing shoes because of the coral and lava rocks. It's quite a walk, but head toward Diamond Head and the public beach areas for better surf. The Ilikai is 40 years old and definelty in need of a face lift. The pool is very small. The hotel has little shade and the sun scorches the tiny balconies and quickly heats up the rooms. Forget sitting on your balcony or opening the curtains in your room until sunset. Our room was not ready and using our Marriott reward points was a big hassle at check-in. This is definelty not the quality you would expect from a Renaissance property. On the positive side, our room was spacious and clean. The restaurant serves a great breakfast buffet.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very Pleased I was surprised the hotel was reasonably priced and is nice... the lobby is nice but not extremely fancy, but the rooms have recently been renovated and the decor is new and very nice. The air conditioning worked well. The bathroom was renovated, but the bathtub/showers are older- but very large and clean. We didn't use the pool, but it looked good. I'm really picky about hotel rooms' cleanliness - and I was pleased with this hotel. The hotel is next to a marina and is on the water, but not the beach. You can easily walk to the beach - about 1/8 mile. I used to live in Hawaii and I recommend you stay in Honolulu, but venture out to other parts of Oahu (and other islands if you can) to get the best vacation. Visit the North Shore (Waimea Beach/Sunset Beach), Kaneohe, Kailua... visit other beaches besides Waikiki (most locals don't even go to Waikiki Beach!!) and do some hiking! It's some of the best hiking in the U.S.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Below Average If you are at all familar with the Renaissance brand of hotels, you will be sorely disappointed. The Renaissance Ilikai is a strange hotel-condo mix...some balconies are cluttered with bikes, bbq's and other junk, so you feel like you are neighbors with a full time resident...which you are.It is a strange concept for a hotel, and it in no way embodies the Renaissance brand. The hotel is in dire need of repair...everything about it is old and decaying.Lobby is nothing special. Hotel feels like one of those giant conference hotels, but this one is half condos, so you feel like you're in a strange pseudo-hotel. The pool and grounds are nothing to ride home about, and the room was what you'd get at Days Inn or Motel 6. I think they are making the televisions in new cars larger than the one that was in our room...if that tells you anything.All in all, I felt like I was in the twilight zone the entire time. The hotel just doen't feel like a hotel. Maybe it is better suited for those guests staying for extended periods of time. The staff were all polite and congenial, though.I was only there for one night, thankfully. If you're like me, and you know what other options exist in Waikiki, you'd be very disappointed when you get to this hotel...trust me, I'm not a picky traveler, but this hotel sucks.For about the same price, go to the Marriott Waikiki Beach Resort at the other end of Waikiki. A much much nicer property, all fresh;y renovated, and in a much nicer part of Waikiki!Stay away from this Renaissance! It's the pits!

<Author>PDLJ
<Content>Ilikai - pluses and minuses Just spent 5 days at the Ilikai attending a convention at the hotel. We were upgraded to a one-bedroom suite in the Yacht Harbor Tower with an ocean view. A beautifully renovated suite with full ocean views from two balconies. Unfortunately, the view of Diamond Head was blocked by the main Ilikai Tower, but the views of the sunsets were incredible.The suite had a cozy bedroom with a queen bed, average-sized bathroom with a tub/shower combination, and a spacious living room with a sofabed. All very fresh and clean. Service was excellent on all fronts with the exception of one concierge (not a regular, I don't think) who didn't know anything about the L'Uraku restaurant and denigrated Japanese restaurants on Kapiolani in general - he couldn't have been more wrong about one of the top-rated restaurants in Honolulu.The hotel's location is not as convenient to Waikiki beach but, quite frankly, Waikiki is overrated and overcrowded as a beach. The hotel is very convenient to the Ala Moana shopping center and its excellent food court. Parking is expensive at $14 a day (self parking - valet parking is $19). Food is expensive and service is slow, but the quality is ok. The business center is a concession and expensive. The two pools are nice, but small.Many of the rooms are owned as condos and serve as year-round residences for the owners. As a result, late night partying is seriously discouraged. Our convention had to shut down a karaoke night by 12:30 and a post-dinner get-together in one of the conference rooms was shut down at 12:30 as well.  
<Date>Nov 17, 2003

<Author>1Travelingon
<Content>It was alright.. This was the second place we stayed, I left a review for our first place the Laie Inn (located on the windward side of island) with TripAdvisor also. Anyway, we stayed here three nights, we got a 45 day advanced purchase price of $120.00 through Expedia for a city view.  We were upgraded to a partial ocean view which both looked over the city and the harbor to your far left. The room was clean and adequate, I would have liked to have had a microwave though. The room is a little worn but not bad. They really gouge you on water though, one bottle is $4.50! The breakfast buffet was $17.95 for adults, we had our 2 children also, so breakfast for all 4 would have been close to $60.00 a day! We chose to eat at a coffee shop across the street from the Hilton Hawaiian Village. The hotel did provide little extra's like Q-tips, shoe polish and cotton balls, and the pool towels were nice and plush, better than the room towels. The lobby is nice, the concierge was very friendly, only one lady was working and we had about a 25 minute wait, but she was very helpful once it was our turn. It is quite a stroll to Waikiki beach, you are hot and tired by the time you get back from the beach. If I had to do it all over again, first of all I would have stayed the entire time on the other side of the Island, but if I had to stay in Waikiki it would be the Hilton Hawaiian Village, our friends stayed there and received (because it was available) a 2 room upgrade, and the village has the ambiance of a tropical island that the CITY of Waikiki is lacking. They have much more to offer, we were trying to save money though, but really because of the location we did a lot of walking which is seriously something to keep in mind if you are handi-capped or out of shape. The buses are $2.00 per adult, per ride and it ads up fast, they have a 4 day pass also, again a family of 4 ends up being around 50-$60.00. On top of that, in order to get to any Hotel you have to pay for a Taxi, Limo or Shuttle, it's not going to be any less than $20.00 one-way. The prices of everything are very high in Waikiki unless you can get to the swap meet at the stadium, a giant flea market had some good deals, but even better is to shop where the locals go all over the rest of the Island. Your best off to hit Wal-Marts and Safeway when you first get there, pick up all your ammenities that are going to cost you twice as much in Waikiki. Hotel parking at the Ilikai is $8 or 9.00 a day, they have Alamo on site. We rented a car for the first 3 days of our trip leaving the airport and paid an extra $30.00 to drop it off at the Ilikai, it was worth it, no hassles, we took a cab back, there was a coupon in the Oahu Gold free coupon book (found most anywhere) for I Do Cab it was $17.00 to the airport, they arrived on time, and we gave him a $20.00 bill total, the least expensive way to go, cabs are usually $25-26.00 to airport before tip. There was nothing really bad or really good about this hotel, most of the clientle was senior citizen while we were there, and they had weddings and group meetings going on all the time in a ballroom, but they are not a bother to the guests, however you have to walk by them while in your swimsuit if your coming from the pool and they are gathered outside smoking or taking a break. Women receive an orchid for their hair upon arrival, there are stores, deli and restaurants (good ratings on food) on site. I was very disappointed in the fact that they advertise a very large lazer tag facility for kids, (this was one of the reasons I chose the Ilikai), however it is closed or by appointment only on Mon-Wed. the days that we were there! My son was really looking forward to it and was extremely disappointed. The pools are not large, but adequate and clean. The whirlpool had some broken jets. The window on our 9th floor room did not lock easily, it was a chensey lock and there is only a bar about a foot high, nothing to stop a small child from falling out, I feel they should have at least one more safety latch. The lobby is open-aired and pretty, as well as directly outside the lobby, pretty but small area, just not alot to offer.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very nice, with a few exceptions. We had 2 rooms at the Ilikai for 2 nights, and had mixed results. One room was a double and the other had a King size bed. Both rooms had a full kitchen, with a full size fridge, oven, microwave, and dishwasher. Large bathroom. Both rooms faced the city, and the view was nice, although you were looking into the condos accross the street. The room with the king size bed had some a/c problems, as it was too noisy and not cooling well, but it was not too big a problem. 2 pools, one heated, and poolside service at both. Waikiki Beach was a short walk past the Hilton. Staff was very friendly and helpful. The hotel is at the far end of the Waikiki beach strip, but within a short walk of everything.
